--- Commit Message ---
LU-10499 pcc: add readonly mode for PCC

Readonly Persistent Client Cache (RO-PCC) shares the same framework
with Readwrite Persistent Client Cache, expect that no HSM mechanism
is used in readonly mode of PCC. Instead, RO-PCC adds a new flag
field in the file object's layout named LCM_FL_PCC_RDONLY to
indicate that the file is in PCC read-only state. It is protected
under the layout lock.

After introducing the readonly feature for the layout, the IO path
has some changes. For read, if the file has been valid RO-PCC
cached, the file data can be read from PCC directly; Otherwise, it
will read data using normal I/O path from OSTs. For data modifying
operations (write or truncate), it must clear the readonly flag of
the layout on MDT (which will invaliate the RO-PCC cached state on
clients via layout lock blocking callback), and then it can perform
I/O.

For RO-PCC, as the PCC cached file is actual a replication of
Lustre file, when data read on PCC failed, it can tolerate this
error by falling back to normal read path: read data from OSTs.

Refer to paper (LPCC: hierarchical persistent client caching for
Lustre) for more design details.

Test-Parameters: clientcount=3 testlist=sanity-pcc,sanity-pcc,sanity-pcc

Patch Set 5:

(3 comments)

--- Message (Li Xi, 2020-05-28 01:52:22.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

> Instead, the PCC-RO state could be stored in the HSM xattr with an HS_PCC_RO flag, similar to HS_ARCHIVED, so that it is kept in the same place as other HSM state used to manage PCC-RW files.

PCC-RO is not using HSM mechanism. That means, if we use HSM xattr to save PCC-RO flag, the xattr needs to be created. It makes sense for PCC-RW to save everything to HSM xattr if possible. But it doesn't look like put PCC-RO flags to HSM xattr.

> There is already a LCM_FL_RDONLY flag there used for the FLR state, and ideally PCC-RO would use the same state machine as FLR.

LCM_FL_RDONLY seems only set the component readonly, not the entire file. When a file is being fetched to PCC-RO, the entire file becomes readonly, meaning: even the file has multiple FLR mirror, if any client wants to edit any FLR mirror, the PCC-RO cache should be invalidated. That means, in order to combin PCC-RO together with FLR, additional logic is needed to insert the PCC-RO cache invalidation process to the process of settting FLR mirrors to stale. That seems a lot of work, and I am not sure how much advatange it will bring to PCC-RO itself.

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2020-05-28 02:19:32.000000000) ---

(3 comments)

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-07-06 21:31:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 13:

(3 comments)

This also needs to update lfsck_layout_verify_header() to handle LFSCK running on a filesystem with this type of layout.

Regarding the use of LOV_MAGIC_FOREIGN, I _think_ that this would reduce the total amount of code in Lustre, because of sharing this layout type with foreign files, rather than adding yet another special case.  However, I haven't looked into this in total detail.  Could you please take a look into whether this is practical to do or not?

The data structures are themselves compatible.  One thing that would need to change is that LOV_MAGIC_FOREIGN layouts should be allowed as a component of the PFL/FLR file rather than only on the top level.

It _may_ be that LOV_MAGIC_FOREIGN has incompatible access semantics if it is the only layout in the file, but at least we could share the code accessing these data structures in the same way, even if there is a different magic, similar to LOV_MAGIC_V1 and LOV_MAGIC_V3.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-12-06 21:41:28.000000000) ---
Patch Set 31:

(3 comments)

This looks like a rebase of the previous patch, but doesn't merge in the multiple fixes present in later PCC-RO patches? Having known bugs fixed in later patches makes it hard to usefully review this patch because there will be several problems found, but we may miss other bugs as a result. 

That doesn't mean I want *all* of the patches merged into this (already very large) patch. Things like "mmap support" and "auto-join" and "improve policy" should be separate patches.  However, the later *fixes* (and any code restructuring) should be merged so that there are not later patches in the series like "rework mmap code", or changes to variable and function names should not be done in later patches.
